(His saying: 'and it is taken from him') i.e., from the need of everything other than Him for Him. (His saying: 'also') i.e., just as what preceded was taken from it. 144 (His saying: 'the occurrence of the world' i.e., everything other than God, may He be exalted, and it is not hidden that this is additional to the creeds, but it is related to them. And the purpose of that is the refutation of the philosophers: they are disbelievers from the Romans, they were from the people of Greece, and they were people of wisdom and intellect, and they engaged in asceticism and renunciation, and their leader was the philosopher. Ibn al-Salah said: he was not a scholar, and when Moses was sent in their time, he called them to his law, but they refused and were arrogant and said: we are independent of what you have, for we say what you say and more. And they said the world is eternal, but they only said the eternity of its origins, which are the four elements: water, earth, air, and fire, not their individuals, and likewise they said the eternity of the celestial spheres. (His saying: 'directly') is a metaphor for the comprehensiveness of the world's occurrence, so its meaning is generalization. (Altogether). Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri. (His saying: 'and likewise if it was not executed... etc.') there is no need for this, because it is a result of what preceded; since when neither their will is executed nor the will of one of them, the necessary consequence is the non-execution of the will of either.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a combined commentary and argument exposition. It begins by explaining a line from al-Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin: 'then nothing is in need of Him' pointing to a second proof for divine unity. The commentator notes that the proof is a conditional syllogism: if there were a second god, nothing would need Him, but everything does need Him, so a second god is impossible. However, al-Bajuri points out a deficiency in this proof: it does not address other quantifiers (perhaps meaning it is not fully formal). Then the text discusses the necessary consequence of two gods: either they agree or disagree. If they agree and act together on one effect, it would be the conjunction of two independent agents on one effect, which is impossible whether simultaneous or sequential. If they disagree and both wills are executed, contradictions arise; if one's will is thwarted, that one is incapable, and then the other must be similar and thus also incapable. The marginal gloss by al-Ajhuri clarifies that the impossibility is specifically when each acts independently, not cooperatively, but divinity requires independence. He also explains that the analogy between them does not prove incapability after execution of will but rather the non-execution of either's will from the outset. On the second page, the text turns to deriving the temporal origination of the world from the same premise of dependence. The world, meaning everything other than God, is argued to be originated (hadith) because it is subject to need. This is used to refute the philosophers (identified as pre-Socratic Greeks) who believed in the eternity of the world's elements and celestial spheres despite their wisdom. A marginal note clarifies that the phrase 'directly' in the text means the occurrence applies to the entire world. Another marginal note by al-Ajhuri dismisses a previous statement about the non-execution of wills as redundant.

Key Terms
القياس الاستثنائي
اجتماع المؤثرين
عجز
مماثلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof against two gods is complete and flawless, but the commentator explicitly notes a logical deficiency.
Correction: Al-Bajuri points out that the proof does not address 'the rest of the quantifiers', meaning it may not be universally valid without further qualification.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the conjunction of two independent agents on one effect impossible?
A) Because it would require cooperation, which is impossible for divinities.
B) Because if simultaneous, it would be the conjunction of two agents on one effect; if sequential, it would be acquisition of the already acquired.
C) Because it would lead to the execution of contradictory wills.
D) Because the proof is deficient and does not apply.

Key Takeaway
The second proof of tawhid uses a conditional syllogism to show that two gods are impossible because they would either coincide impossibly or one would be incapable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself relying on something or someone other than Allah, as if it shares His power of causation? In what subtle ways might you be associating partners with Him in your heart, even while your tongue declares His oneness? Take time today to repent and realign your trust exclusively to Him.
?
This proof shows that two gods cannot exist because they would either conflict or be dependent. Examine your own life: Are there areas where you try to serve two masters—seeking approval from both Allah and people? How does this realization push you to purify your intentions solely for Allah?
?
If you truly believe that no effect can be produced without Allah’s sole action, how does that change the way you view your own efforts and achievements? Will you attribute your successes to Him alone and your failures as lessons from Him? Make a concrete commitment to recognize His sole agency in every outcome today.

Deriving the World's Createdness and Refuting the Philosophers
Al-Bajuri derives the world's createdness from the premise of dependence and uses it to refute the philosophers' belief in eternal elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Bajuri derives the temporal origination of the world from the premise that everything depends on God, and how this refutes the philosophers' claim that the world's elements are eternal.

Core Idea
The world's dependence on God proves it is created, contradicting the philosophers' belief in eternal elements.

After establishing that everything other than God depends on Him, al-Bajuri extracts a further conclusion: the world is temporally originated (hadith). He then explains that this refutes the ancient Greek philosophers who, despite their wisdom, believed in the eternity of the four elements and the celestial spheres. This lesson traces that argument and its historical context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the derivation
Find where al-Bajuri says 'ويؤخذ منه' (and it is taken from him) to see how the createdness of the world is derived from the general dependence of everything on God.
The derivation is an additional point beyond the creeds (عقائد).
2
Understand the philosophers' view
Read the description of the philosophers: they were Greek, wise, ascetic, but rejected Moses' call. They believed the world is eternal in its origins (elements and spheres), not in its individuals.
The text identifies them as Romans (يونان) and mentions their leader was called 'the philosopher'.
3
See the refutation's purpose
The purpose of deriving createdness is to refute the philosophers' claim. Note that the refutation targets their belief in eternal elements, not individuals.
The marginal note on 'باشره' indicates the createdness applies to the entire world, not just parts.

(وقوله: أَيْضاً) أي: كما أُخِذَ منه ما تقدم. 144 (وقوله: حُدُوتُ الْعَالَمِ أي ما سِوَى الله تعالى ولا يخفى أن هذا زائد على العقائد، لكنه مما يتعلَّق بها. والغَرَضُ من ذلك: الرَّدُّ على الفلاسفة: وهم كُفَّارٌ من الروم، كانوا من أهل يُونَانَ، وكانوا أَهْلَ حكمةٍ وعَقْل، وأخذوا في التَّرَيضِ والتزهد، وكان رئيسهم الفيلسوف. قال ابن الصلاح) : ولم يكن عالماً، ولما بُعِثَ موسى في زمانهم دعاهم إلى شريعته، فأبوا واستكبروا وقالوا: نحن في غنية عما عندك، فإنا نقول بما تقول وزيادةً، وقد قالوا بقدم العالم، لكن إنما قالوا بقدَم أصوله، وهي العناصر الأربع): الماء والتراب والهواء والنارُ دونَ أشخاصه، وكذا قالوا بقدَمِ الأفلاك (قوله: باشره) هو كناية عن شُمُول الحدوث للعالم كله، فمعناه التعميم. بِأَسْرِه) حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وَكَذَا لَوْ لَمْ يَنْفُذ... إلخ) هذا لا حاجة إليه؛ لأنه نتيجة ما قبله؛ لأنهما حيث لم ينفذ مرادهما ولا مراد أحدهما فاللازم على ذلك: عدم نفوذ مراد واحد منهما.
Gloss of al-Bajuri on al-Sanusi. (His saying: 'then nothing is in need of Him' therein is an indication of the second proof, and its exposition has preceded). (His saying: 'How, and He is the One to whom everything other than Him is in need') has been discussed many times, so do not be heedless. (His saying: 'And He also necessitates for Him, exalted') i.e., just as He necessitated what preceded. (His saying: 'For if there were a second in divinity with Him, nothing would be in need... etc.') he indicated by that a conditional syllogism, its arrangement is thus: If there were a second in divinity with Him, nothing would be in need of Him, but the non-need of anything of Him is false, for how can it be when He is the One to whom everything other than Him is in need? And it is not hidden what deficiency is in this proof, due to lack of addressing the rest of the quantifiers. (His saying: 'Due to the necessitation of their incapability then' i.e., when there is a second in divinity with Him. And the aspect of the necessitation of their incapability then is because it is not free: either they agree or they differ, and in each case their incapability is necessitated. As for the first, because it necessitates the conjunction of two agents upon one effect if they produce it together, and the acquisition of what is already acquired if they produce it in sequence. As for the second, because it necessitates the conjunction of two contradictories if both their wills are executed, and if the will of one is executed and not the other, the one whose will is not executed is incapable, and the other is likewise, due to the analogy between them. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri. (His saying: 'conjunction of two agents upon one effect' i.e., in the manner of each independently producing that effect; for this is what is judged impossible, unlike their conjunction upon it by way of assistance, for that is possible, but divinity precludes that and necessitates that each one produces it independently, and you have known that producing it in this manner is impossible. (His saying: 'then the other is likewise' judging him with incapability despite the execution of his will is unintelligible. (His saying: 'due to the analogy between them' does not produce his incapability after the execution of his will, but rather produces the non-execution of the will of either initially, and when neither their will is executed due to what necessitates the conjunction of contradictories, nor the will of one due to the analogy between them, their incapability is determined. Scanned by CamScanner. Text of Umm al-Barahin by Abu Abdullah al-Sanusi. Then their incapability is established, and likewise if the will of each were not executed as is apparent. (His saying: 'and it is taken from him') i.e., from the need of everything other than Him for Him. (His saying: 'also') i.e., just as what preceded was taken from it. 144 (His saying: 'the occurrence of the world' i.e., everything other than God, may He be exalted, and it is not hidden that this is additional to the creeds, but it is related to them. And the purpose of that is the refutation of the philosophers: they are disbelievers from the Romans, they were from the people of Greece, and they were people of wisdom and intellect, and they engaged in asceticism and renunciation, and their leader was the philosopher. Ibn al-Salah said: he was not a scholar, and when Moses was sent in their time, he called them to his law, but they refused and were arrogant and said: we are independent of what you have, for we say what you say and more. And they said the world is eternal, but they only said the eternity of its origins, which are the four elements: water, earth, air, and fire, not their individuals, and likewise they said the eternity of the celestial spheres. (His saying: 'directly') is a metaphor for the comprehensiveness of the world's occurrence, so its meaning is generalization. (Altogether). Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri. (His saying: 'and likewise if it was not executed... etc.') there is no need for this, because it is a result of what preceded; since when neither their will is executed nor the will of one of them, the necessary consequence is the non-execution of the will of either.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a combined commentary and argument exposition. It begins by explaining a line from al-Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin: 'then nothing is in need of Him' pointing to a second proof for divine unity. The commentator notes that the proof is a conditional syllogism: if there were a second god, nothing would need Him, but everything does need Him, so a second god is impossible. However, al-Bajuri points out a deficiency in this proof: it does not address other quantifiers (perhaps meaning it is not fully formal). Then the text discusses the necessary consequence of two gods: either they agree or disagree. If they agree and act together on one effect, it would be the conjunction of two independent agents on one effect, which is impossible whether simultaneous or sequential. If they disagree and both wills are executed, contradictions arise; if one's will is thwarted, that one is incapable, and then the other must be similar and thus also incapable. The marginal gloss by al-Ajhuri clarifies that the impossibility is specifically when each acts independently, not cooperatively, but divinity requires independence. He also explains that the analogy between them does not prove incapability after execution of will but rather the non-execution of either's will from the outset. On the second page, the text turns to deriving the temporal origination of the world from the same premise of dependence. The world, meaning everything other than God, is argued to be originated (hadith) because it is subject to need. This is used to refute the philosophers (identified as pre-Socratic Greeks) who believed in the eternity of the world's elements and celestial spheres despite their wisdom. A marginal note clarifies that the phrase 'directly' in the text means the occurrence applies to the entire world. Another marginal note by al-Ajhuri dismisses a previous statement about the non-execution of wills as redundant.

Key Terms
حدوث العالم
الفلاسفة
قدم العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the philosophers believed in the absolute eternity of the world, but they only claimed eternity of elements and spheres, not individuals.
Correction: The text explicitly says they said the world is eternal 'but they only said the eternity of its origins, which are the four elements... not their individuals.'

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what exactly did the philosophers claim to be eternal?
A) The entire world including all its individuals.
B) The four elements and the celestial spheres, but not individual entities.
C) Only the celestial spheres.
D) Only the human soul.

Key Takeaway
The world's dependence on God proves it is created, refuting the Greek philosophers who believed only in the eternity of elements and spheres.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on your own intellect to reject a truth from revelation, similar to how the philosophers rejected Moses because they thought they had superior knowledge? In what area of your life do you need to submit your reasoning to God's word?
?
The philosophers were described as wise, intellectual, and ascetic, yet they were disbelievers. Do you measure spiritual worth by intelligence or devotion rather than submission to the truth? How can you guard against pride in your own understanding?
?
If the createdness of the world is a derived conclusion rather than a direct article of faith, does that make it less important? Will you live today with the conviction that everything other than God depends on Him, and therefore you are completely reliant on your Creator?

Sanusi's Direct Explanation of 'Generally and in Every State'
Sanusi defines his phrase in terms of essences and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's intended meaning of the phrase 'عمومًا وعلى كل حال' as it applies to all essences and all attributes.

Core Idea
Sanusi's phrase means the possible being needs God in every respect.

In this passage, Sanusi directly answers a question about what he meant by 'generally and in every state'. His answer is simple but profound: 'generally' refers to all essences, and 'in every state' refers to all attributes. This clarifies that the possible being's dependence on God is universal, covering both its essence and all its attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the Arabic passage once. Note that Sanusi is being asked to explain his own phrase.
This is a rare moment where the author clarifies his own wording.
2
Identify the two parts of the answer
Notice that Sanusi divides his answer into two: 'عمومًا' for essences and 'على كل حال' for attributes. Understand what each covers.
All possible essences and all their attributes are included.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why clarifying that dependence covers both essence and attributes is important for the overall argument about divine independence.
It emphasizes that nothing about the possible being is independent of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: عُمُوماً وَعَلَى كُلِّ حَالٍ لم يتعرض المصنف لذلك في شرحه، لكنه سُئِلَ عن ذلك، فقيل له: ما أردتَ بقولك: عموماً وعلى كل حال؟ فقال: عموماً في جميع الذوات، وعلى كل حال في جميع الصفات. اهـ.
وحينئذ فالحمل على ذلك لكونه أراده المصنفُ أَوْلى؛ وإِن أَمْكَنَ تفسيرُهما بغير ذلك، كأن يقال: عموماً أي سواءً كان مما يقارِنُه سبب عادي كالشَّبَع والرِّيّ أو لا كخلق السماء والأرض، وعلى كلّ حالٍ :أي من حالتي الوجود والعدم، فالممكن يفتقر إليه تعالى في الحالتين، أما في حالة العدم؛ فلأنه يحتاج إليه تعالى في إيجاده وأما في حالة الوجود؛ فلأنا إن قلنا بأن العَرَضَ لا يبقى زمانين؛ افْتَقَرَ الممكن إليه تعالى في إمدادِ ذاته بالأعراض التي لولا تعاقبها عليها لانعدمت، وإن قلنا بأن العَرَضَ يبقى زمانين فأكثرَ - وهو الراجح - ؛ افتقر الممكنُ إليه تعالى أيضاً في دوام وجوده، بناءً على المختار من أن منشأ افتقار الممكن الإمكان، أي: استواءُ نِسْبَتَى الوجود والعدم إليه بالنظر لذاته؛ لأن هذا الوصف لا يُفَارِقُهُ، فيكون مفتقراً إليه تعالى كل لحظةٍ في ترجيح وجوده على عدمه، وأما على مقابله من أن مَنْشَأ افتقاره الحدوث - أي: الوجودُ بعد عَدَمٍ ؛ فلا يفتقرُ إليه تعالى في دوام وجوده ضرورة أن هذا الوصف - أعني : الوجود بعد عدم - قد حَصَلَ، فلو احتاج إليه بعد حصوله؛ لَزِمَ تحصيل الحاصل.
(His statement: generally and in every state. The author did not mention that in his commentary, but he was asked about it, so it was said to him: What did you mean by your statement: 'generally and in every state'? He said: 'Generally' regarding all essences, and 'in every state' regarding all attributes. End.) And then carrying this upon that because the author intended it is more appropriate; even if it is possible to interpret them otherwise, such as saying: 'generally' meaning whether it is accompanied by a customary cause like satiety and thirst or not, like the creation of the heavens and earth; and 'in every state' meaning in the states of existence and non-existence; the possible (al-mumkin) is in need of Him in both states. As for the state of non-existence, because it needs Him for its existence; and as for the state of existence, because if we say that the accident does not survive two moments, then the possible is in need of Him in the supply of its essence with accidents that, if they did not succeed one another, it would cease to exist; and if we say that the accident survives two moments or more—and that is the preponderant view—then the possible is still in need of Him for the continuation of its existence, based on the chosen view that the source of the possible's need is possibility (al-imkān), i.e., the equal relation of existence and non-existence to it by itself; because this description never leaves it, so it is in need of Him every moment for the preponderance of its existence over non-existence. And on the opposite view that the source of its need is origination (al-ḥudūth)—i.e., existence after non-existence—then it does not need Him for the continuation of its existence, necessarily because this description—namely, existence after non-existence—has already occurred; so if it needed Him after its occurrence, it would necessitate the acquisition of what is already acquired.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of Sanusi's phrase 'عمومًا وعلى كل حال'. Sanusi himself explained that 'عمومًا' means all essences, and 'على كل حال' means all attributes. But Bajuri notes that it can also be interpreted as covering all possible beings whether accompanied by customary causes or not, and in both states of existence and non-existence. Then Bajuri launches into a detailed discussion of the basis of the possible's need for God: is it because of possibility (al-imkān) or because of origination (al-ḥudūth)? He discusses two views on the survival of accidents, and argues that even if accidents survive, the possible is still in need because possibility is inherent. This is a sophisticated argument about divine independence.

Key Terms
عموماً
على كل حال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the need only applies to the essence, not attributes.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly says it covers both essences and attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does 'عمومًا' refer to?
A) All essences
B) All attributes
C) All states
D) All causes

Key Takeaway
Sanusi intended his phrase to mean that the possible being is dependent on God in its very essence and all its attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that your very essence and every attribute depend entirely on Allah at every moment. Which attribute—such as your intelligence, health, or patience—do you most often act as if you own independently? What specific thought or action can you use today to remind yourself that it is a gift?
?
If 'every state' includes even your private thoughts and intentions, in what area of your inner life do you resist surrendering to Allah's control? Will you commit to turning that area over to Him in prayer right now?
?
Sanusi's definition leaves no room for any part of you that is self-sufficient. Which part of your life—your career, relationships, or identity—do you fear would collapse if you fully admitted your total need for God? How can you begin to trust Him with that fear today?

The Basis of the Possible's Continuous Need for God
Bajuri discusses alternative interpretation and the ground of the possible's continuous need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasoning behind why the possible being needs God not only for creation but also for its continued existence, and the debate between possibility (imkān) and origination (ḥudūth) as the basis of need.

Core Idea
The possible being's inherent possibility necessitates God's continuous support.

Building on Sanusi's clarification, Bajuri explores an alternative interpretation and then dives into the philosophical foundation of the possible's need for God. He discusses whether the need arises from possibility inherent in the essence or from the fact of origination, and whether accidents survive. This lesson unpacks that intricate argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the alternative interpretation
Read the first part of the passage where Bajuri presents another way to interpret 'عمومًا' and 'على كل حال' involving customary causes and states of existence.
This interpretation is possible but not the primary one.
2
Grasp the need in both states
Notice that the possible needs God in both non-existence (for creation) and in existence (for continuation).
The need is not limited to the moment of creation.
3
Contrast the two views on accident survival
Identify the two views: that accidents do not survive two moments, and that they do. See how each leads to a need for God's continuous involvement.
Even if accidents survive, the need remains due to possibility.
4
Understand the source of need: possibility vs. origination
Focus on the argument that the source of need is possibility (imkān), which never leaves the possible, rather than origination (ḥudūth), which only occurs at the beginning.
This is the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: عُمُوماً وَعَلَى كُلِّ حَالٍ لم يتعرض المصنف لذلك في شرحه، لكنه سُئِلَ عن ذلك، فقيل له: ما أردتَ بقولك: عموماً وعلى كل حال؟ فقال: عموماً في جميع الذوات، وعلى كل حال في جميع الصفات. اهـ.
وحينئذ فالحمل على ذلك لكونه أراده المصنفُ أَوْلى؛ وإِن أَمْكَنَ تفسيرُهما بغير ذلك، كأن يقال: عموماً أي سواءً كان مما يقارِنُه سبب عادي كالشَّبَع والرِّيّ أو لا كخلق السماء والأرض، وعلى كلّ حالٍ :أي من حالتي الوجود والعدم، فالممكن يفتقر إليه تعالى في الحالتين، أما في حالة العدم؛ فلأنه يحتاج إليه تعالى في إيجاده وأما في حالة الوجود؛ فلأنا إن قلنا بأن العَرَضَ لا يبقى زمانين؛ افْتَقَرَ الممكن إليه تعالى في إمدادِ ذاته بالأعراض التي لولا تعاقبها عليها لانعدمت، وإن قلنا بأن العَرَضَ يبقى زمانين فأكثرَ - وهو الراجح - ؛ افتقر الممكنُ إليه تعالى أيضاً في دوام وجوده، بناءً على المختار من أن منشأ افتقار الممكن الإمكان، أي: استواءُ نِسْبَتَى الوجود والعدم إليه بالنظر لذاته؛ لأن هذا الوصف لا يُفَارِقُهُ، فيكون مفتقراً إليه تعالى كل لحظةٍ في ترجيح وجوده على عدمه، وأما على مقابله من أن مَنْشَأ افتقاره الحدوث - أي: الوجودُ بعد عَدَمٍ ؛ فلا يفتقرُ إليه تعالى في دوام وجوده ضرورة أن هذا الوصف - أعني : الوجود بعد عدم - قد حَصَلَ، فلو احتاج إليه بعد حصوله؛ لَزِمَ تحصيل الحاصل.
(His statement: generally and in every state. The author did not mention that in his commentary, but he was asked about it, so it was said to him: What did you mean by your statement: 'generally and in every state'? He said: 'Generally' regarding all essences, and 'in every state' regarding all attributes. End.) And then carrying this upon that because the author intended it is more appropriate; even if it is possible to interpret them otherwise, such as saying: 'generally' meaning whether it is accompanied by a customary cause like satiety and thirst or not, like the creation of the heavens and earth; and 'in every state' meaning in the states of existence and non-existence; the possible (al-mumkin) is in need of Him in both states. As for the state of non-existence, because it needs Him for its existence; and as for the state of existence, because if we say that the accident does not survive two moments, then the possible is in need of Him in the supply of its essence with accidents that, if they did not succeed one another, it would cease to exist; and if we say that the accident survives two moments or more—and that is the preponderant view—then the possible is still in need of Him for the continuation of its existence, based on the chosen view that the source of the possible's need is possibility (al-imkān), i.e., the equal relation of existence and non-existence to it by itself; because this description never leaves it, so it is in need of Him every moment for the preponderance of its existence over non-existence. And on the opposite view that the source of its need is origination (al-ḥudūth)—i.e., existence after non-existence—then it does not need Him for the continuation of its existence, necessarily because this description—namely, existence after non-existence—has already occurred; so if it needed Him after its occurrence, it would necessitate the acquisition of what is already acquired.

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of Sanusi's phrase 'عمومًا وعلى كل حال'. Sanusi himself explained that 'عمومًا' means all essences, and 'على كل حال' means all attributes. But Bajuri notes that it can also be interpreted as covering all possible beings whether accompanied by customary causes or not, and in both states of existence and non-existence. He discusses two views on the survival of accidents, and argues that even if accidents survive, the possible is still in need because possibility is inherent. This is a sophisticated argument about divine independence.

Key Takeaway

?

?

?

The Impossibility of Influence by Nature (Tab')
Al-Bajuri explains the impossibility of influence by nature and its logical consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hypothesis that a creature influences by its own nature (tab') is impossible and what it implies about God's independence.

Core Idea
If creatures influenced by nature, effects would be independent of God—impossible.

Al-Bajuri begins by clarifying the meaning of 'impossible' in the earlier text. He explains that influence by a God-given power is one thing, but influence by nature is another. This lesson unpacks the first supposition to show why it leads to a logical contradiction, emphasizing that everything depends on God alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Bajuri sets up the context.
The phrase 'so that is impossible' refers to influence by a God-given power, but he also applies it to natural influence.
2
Identify the first supposition
Find where Al-Bajuri says 'if you suppose that the influence of a thing from the created things is by its nature'. This is the hypothesis he examines.
3
Understand the logical consequence
Al-Bajuri argues that if natural influence were possible, the effect would be independent of God. Ask yourself: why is that impossible? Because all else depends on God.
This reasoning shows that the impossibility is logical, not just a decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: فَذَلِكَ مُحَالٌ) جواب (أما)، واسمُ الإشارة عائد لكون شيء من الكائنات مؤثِراً بقوَّةٍ جعلها الله تعالى فيه.
:(وقوله أَيضاً) أي: كما أن كَوْنَ شيءٍ منها مؤثراً بطبعه محال. وحق المقابلة أن يقول فلا يكون عدمه مأخوذاً من افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه تعالى، بل من استغنائه جل وعز عن كل ما سواه كما هو ظاهر.
والحاصل : أنه إن قَدَّرْتَ أن تأثير شيءٍ من الكائنات بطبعه؛ فعدمه مأخوذ من افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه تعالى، وإلا ; لَزِمَ أن يستغني ذلك الأثر عن مولانا جل وعزَّ، كيف وهو الذي يَفْتَقِرُ إليه كلُّ ما سواه، وإن قَدَّرْتَ أن تأثير شيءٍ من الكائنات بقوَّةٍ جَعَلَها الله تعالى فيه؛ فعدمُهُ مأخوذ من استغنائه تعالى عن كل ما سواه، وإلا; لَزِمَ افتقارُهُ في إيجادِ بعض الأفعال إلى واسطةٍ، كيف وهو جَلَّ وعز الغني عن كلّ ما سواه.
والفرقُ بين هذين التقديرين: أن التأثير في الأول لا يتوقف على مشيئة الله تعالى واختياره؛ لأن ما كان بالطبع لا يتوقف على ذلك، فلَزِمَ فيه أن الأثر مستغن عن الله تعالى، ولم يَلْزَمِ افتقارهُ تعالى إلى واسطةٍ بخلافه في الثاني، فإنه يتوقف على مشيئة الله تعالى واختياره حتى يَخْلُقَ القوَّةَ في الأسباب العادية، فصار الفعل من هذه الحيثية مُرَاداً لله تعالى، ولزم افتقارُهُ في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة، ولم يَلْزَمْ أن الأَثَرَ مستغن عن الله تعالى. فتدبر.
His statement: 'So that is impossible' is the answer to 'as for', and the demonstrative pronoun refers to the fact that a thing from the created things can be influential by a power that God Almighty placed in it. And his statement 'also' means: just as the fact that a thing from them is influential by its nature is impossible. And the correct contrast is that one should say: so its non-existence is not taken from the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, but rather from His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, as is apparent. The conclusion: if you suppose that the influence of a thing from the created things is by its nature, then its non-existence is taken from the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, otherwise it would necessitate that that effect is self-sufficient from our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, despite the fact that everything other than Him depends upon Him. And if you suppose that the influence of a thing from the created things is by a power that God Almighty placed in it, then its non-existence is taken from His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, otherwise it would necessitate His dependence in the creation of some actions upon a medium, despite the fact that He, Glorified and Exalted, is the Self-sufficient from everything other than Him. The difference between these two suppositions: that the influence in the first does not depend on the will and choice of God Almighty, because that which is by nature does not depend on that, so it necessitates in it that the effect is self-sufficient from God Almighty, and it does not necessitate His dependence upon a medium. Contrary to the second, because it depends on the will and choice of God Almighty until He creates the power in the customary causes, so the action from this perspective becomes desired by God Almighty, and it necessitates His dependence in the creation of some actions upon a medium, and it does not necessitate that the effect is self-sufficient from God Almighty. So reflect.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definition and comparative analysis of two types of created influence (tathir). Al-Bajuri explains that the phrase 'so that is impossible' answers the conditional 'as for'. He clarifies that the impossibility applies to the scenario where a creature influences by its own nature (bi-tab'ih). In contrast, the correct understanding is that a creature's non-existence is derived not from the dependence of all else on God, but from God's self-sufficiency (istighna'). He then presents two suppositions: (1) influence by nature – if a creature influenced by its nature, that would imply the effect is independent of God, which is impossible because all else depends on Him; (2) influence by a power God placed in it – if a creature influences by a God-given power, then its non-existence is taken from God's self-sufficiency, otherwise God would depend on a medium (wastia) for some actions, contradicting His absolute independence. The key difference is that influence by nature does not depend on God's will, so the effect becomes independent. Influence by a God-given power depends on God's will, making the action willed by God, but it introduces a medium. Al-Bajuri concludes by urging reflection (tadabbur).

Key Terms
طبع (tab')
تأثير (tathir)
استغناء (istighna')
افتقار (iftiqar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility of influence by nature is an arbitrary divine decree.
Correction: The passage shows it is a logical impossibility: it would imply the effect is independent of God, contradicting the fact that everything depends on Him.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, what would happen if a creature influences by its nature and its non-existence is not taken from the dependence of all else on God?
A) The effect would be independent of God.
B) God would depend on a medium.
C) The creature would be equal to God.
D) It would be impossible to say.

Key Takeaway
Influence by nature is impossible because it would make the effect independent of God, contradicting the absolute dependence of everything on Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every effect in your life comes directly from God, or do you secretly attribute outcomes to 'nature' or 'circumstance'? What would change if you really lived as if only God is effective?
?
If you claim that nothing influences by its own nature, why do you still fear creatures as if they have independent power? Isn't that a contradiction in your heart?
?
The passage says that influence by nature would make the effect independent of God. Is there any area of your life where you act as if you are independent of God, relying on your own nature or abilities? What step can you take today to acknowledge your absolute dependence?

Influence by God-Given Power and the Difference from Natural Influence
Al-Bajuri presents the second supposition and compares it with the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second supposition of created influence (by a God-given power) and how it differs from natural influence in its implications for God's independence.

Core Idea
Influence by God-given power depends on God's will, preserving His independence while allowing secondary causation.

After explaining the impossibility of natural influence, Al-Bajuri now examines the second supposition: influence by a power that God places in the creature. He shows that this scenario leads to a different problem—that God would depend on a medium—unless we correctly derive nonexistence from His self-sufficiency. He then contrasts the two suppositions, highlighting their distinct logical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the shift to the second supposition and the comparison.
The passage begins with 'And if you suppose'.
2
Understand the second supposition
Identify the hypothesis: influence by a power God placed in the creature. Note the consequence if its non-existence is not taken from God's self-sufficiency: God would depend on a medium.
3
Grasp the difference between the two
Al-Bajuri explains that natural influence does not depend on God's will, making the effect independent; influence by power depends on God's will, making the action willed by God but introducing a medium.
This shows that the impossibility of the second is removed by deriving non-existence from self-sufficiency.

Source Text

?

The Syllogism Against Created Influence
Al-Bajuri explains the syllogism against created influence with its two premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical syllogism that refutes the idea that creatures can influence by a power God placed in them, and how it confirms God's independence from all mediums.

Core Idea
No creature can influence even with God-given power—God needs no medium.

Al-Bajuri unpacks a tight syllogism embedded in Sanusi's text. It may look simple, but it cuts to the heart of Islamic causality: if creatures could influence by a God-given power, God would become dependent on a medium. Since dependence is impossible for God, such influence is impossible. This lesson walks through the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two premises
Read the passage and locate the major premise (kubra) and minor premise (sughra). Notice how Al-Bajuri extracts them from the text.
The major is a conditional; the minor denies its consequent.
2
Understand the consequence
The major says: if a creature influences by God-given power, then God becomes dependent on a medium. Ask: why would that be a problem?
3
See the minor premise's proof
Al-Bajuri indicates that the minor premise (God's dependence is false) is proven by the earlier discussion of God's self-sufficiency. Look at how that connects.
4
Check your understanding
Do you see why this syllogism refutes the idea of independent secondary causation? Consider what would happen if the conclusion were false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: لِأَنَّهُ :أي: الحالُ والشأن.
(وقوله: يَصِيرُ حِينَئِذٍ أي حين إذ قَدَّرْته مؤثراً بقوةٍ جعلها الله فيه، ويُؤخَذُ من ذلك كُبْرَى القياس القائلة: لو قدَّرْتَ أن شيئاً من الكائنات يؤثِرُ بقوَّةٍ جعلها الله تعالى فيه لصار حينئذٍ مولانا جل وعز مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة، وقد أشار بقوله : ( وذلك باطل إلى صُغْرَاه القائلة: لكن كونه جل وعز يصيرُ مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة باطل، ثم عَلَّل ذلك بقوله: (لما عرفت... إلخ)، فصار نَظْمُ القياس هكذا: لو قَدَّرْتَ أن شيئاً من الكائنات يؤثر بقوةٍ جعلها الله تعالى فيه لصار حينئذ مولانا جل وعز مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة، لكن كونه جل وعز يصير مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطةٍ باطل لما عرفت... إلخ. (قوله: فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ... إلخ) مفرَّعٌ عن البيان السابق من قوله: (أما استغناؤه جل وعز عن كل ما سواه إلى هنا.
(قوله: تَضَمُّنَ قَوْلِ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا الله أي: تضمنَ معنى قول: لا إله إلا الله، على تقدير المضاف؛ لأن المتضمّن لذلك إنما هو المعنى لا اللفظ كما عُلِمَ مما مَرَّ. والمراد بتضمن المعنى لذلك كَوْنُه بحيث يُؤْخَذُ منه على ما تقدم بيانه، وليس المراد به دلالةَ التضمن التي هي دلالة اللفظ على جزء المعنى كما لا يخفى. (قوله: لِلْأَقْسَامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ) أي: لأنه قد اندرج تحت استغنائه تعالى عن كلّ ما سواه أَحَدَ عَشَرَ من الواجبات وهي الوجود والقدم، والبقاء، والمخالفة للحوادث والقيام بالنفس والسَّمْعُ والبصر والكلام ولوازمها كما أشار لذلك المصنف فيما تقدم بقوله: (أما استغناؤه جل وعز عن كل ما سواه فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى الوجود والقدم... إلخ)، وقد اندرج تحت افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه باقيها كما أشار إليه فيما تقدم بقوله: (وأما افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه جل وعز فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى الحياة... إلخ)، ومعلوم أنه إذا وَجَبَتْ هذه الصفاتُ استحالَتْ أضدادها، وقد اندرج أيضاً تحت الاستغناء الجائز كما أشار إليه فيما تقدم بقوله: (ويؤخذ منه أيضاً أنه لا يجب عليه تعالى فعل شيء من الممكنات... إلخ). فتدبر.
His statement: 'Because' – meaning the state and affair. And his statement: 'He would then become' – meaning when you have supposed it influential by a power that God placed in it. And from that is taken the major premise of the syllogism: If you suppose that something from created things is influential by a power that God Almighty placed in it, then at that time our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium. And he indicated by his statement: 'And that is false' – to its minor premise stating: but His being, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium is false. Then he explained that by his statement: 'because you have known... etc.' So the arrangement of the syllogism becomes: If you suppose that something from created things is influential by a power that God Almighty placed in it, then at that time our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium, but His being, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium is false because you have known... etc. His statement: 'So it has become clear to you... etc.' is a branch of the previous explanation from his statement: 'As for His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him' up to here. His statement: 'the inclusion of the statement: there is no god except Allah' – meaning the inclusion of the meaning of the statement 'there is no god except Allah', on the assumption of the deleted noun; because that which includes it is only the meaning, not the wording, as is known from what has preceded. And what is meant by the inclusion of the meaning for that is its being such that it is taken from it according to what has preceded in its explanation, and it is not meant by it the 'inclusion' signification (dalalat al-tadamun) which is the signification of the wording upon part of the meaning, as is not hidden. His statement: 'for the three divisions' – meaning: because under His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, eleven of the necessary attributes have been subsumed: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, otherness from originated things, self-subsistence, hearing, sight, speech, and their consequences, as the author indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'As for His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, it necessitates for Him, Exalted, existence, pre-eternity... etc.' And under the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, the rest of them have been subsumed, as he indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'As for the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, Glorified and Exalted, it necessitates for Him, Exalted, life... etc.' And it is known that when these attributes are necessary, their opposites become impossible. And also under the permissible self-sufficiency have been subsumed, as he indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'And from it is also taken that it is not obligatory upon Him, Exalted, to do anything from the possible things... etc.' So reflect.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides a logical proof (qiyas) and a doctrinal derivation. First, Al-Bajuri explains the syllogism implicit in Sanusi's text: The major premise (kubra) is that if a creature influences by a God-given power, then God would become dependent on a medium for some actions. The minor premise (sughra) is that God being dependent on a medium is false (bāṭil). The conclusion is that such influence is impossible. Al-Bajuri notes that Sanusi's statement 'because you have known...' provides the justification for the minor premise. Then, Al-Bajuri turns to the phrase 'the inclusion (tadammun) of the statement: there is no god except Allah'. He clarifies that it is the meaning of the shahada, not the wording, that entails the three divisions (aqsām thalātha). This inclusion (tadammun) is not the linguistic signification of part of the meaning, but rather a logical entailment. Specifically, from God's self-sufficiency (istighnā') eleven necessary attributes are derived: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, otherness from originated things, self-subsistence, hearing, sight, speech, and their consequences. From the dependence of all else (iftiqār) on God, the remaining attributes (like life, will, power) are derived. When these attributes are necessary, their opposites become impossible. Additionally, from the permissible (jā'iz) aspect of the shahada, it follows that God is not obligated to do anything possible. Al-Bajuri concludes with 'So reflect' (fa-tadabbar), inviting the reader to contemplate the comprehensiveness of tawhid.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas)
كبرى (kubra)
صغرى (sughra)
واسطة (wasita)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minor premise (sughra) of the syllogism according to Al-Bajuri?
A) If a creature influences by a God-given power, God depends on a medium.
B) God being dependent on a medium is false.
C) Creatures cannot influence by nature.
D) God is self-sufficient from all things.

Key Takeaway
The syllogism shows that positing any created influence by a God-given power leads to the impossible consequence of God's dependence, thus such influence is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'I did that' rather than 'God enabled that'? How does the logical conclusion of this syllogism—that no creature can truly influence anything—challenge your daily sense of self-sufficiency? Will you commit today to mentally attribute every outcome to God alone, even the ones that feel like your own achievement?
?
Reflect on a time you felt you were the 'cause' of someone else's benefit or harm. How does the impossibility of created influence reframe that event? If God is the only real agent, how should that change your interactions with others, especially in terms of humility and reliance on God?
?
The syllogism's minor premise is that God being dependent on a medium is false. Do you ever act as if God needs your cooperation to bring about good in the world? How does this passage purge your heart of hidden arrogance? What practical step will you take today to live in full awareness that God is the sole creator of all actions?

Three Divisions of Tawhid from the Shahada
Al-Bajuri explains the three divisions subsumed under the shahada and their corresponding attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the meaning of 'There is no god except Allah' entails three divisions—necessary, impossible, and permissible—and how specific divine attributes are derived from each.

Core Idea
The shahada logically yields three categories: what God must be, cannot be, and may do.

Al-Bajuri explains that the shahada's meaning, not its wording, includes the three divisions of tawhid. From God's self-sufficiency (istighna') come eleven necessary attributes; from the dependence of all else (iftiqar) come the rest; and from the permissible aspect comes that God is not obligated to do anything. This lesson unpacks that elegant derivation.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'inclusion' (tadammun)
Al-Bajuri clarifies that it is the meaning of the shahada, not the word itself, that entails the three divisions. This is a logical implication, not a linguistic part-whole relation.
Do not confuse with dalalat al-tadammun in language.
2
Identify the three divisions
The three divisions are: 1) what is necessary (wajib) for God, 2) what is impossible (mustahil) for God, and 3) what is permissible (ja'iz) regarding God. Locate how each is derived.
3
Map attributes to each division
Note that eleven attributes (existence, pre-eternity, etc.) come under God's self-sufficiency; the remaining attributes (life, will, power) come under the dependence of creation; and the permissible aspect yields that God is not obligated to create anything.
The opposites of necessary attributes become impossible.
4
Reflect on the comprehensiveness
Al-Bajuri ends with 'fa-tadabbar' (so reflect). Think about how the entire creed of attributes is encapsulated in the simple statement of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: لِأَنَّهُ :أي: الحالُ والشأن.
(وقوله: يَصِيرُ حِينَئِذٍ أي حين إذ قَدَّرْته مؤثراً بقوةٍ جعلها الله فيه، ويُؤخَذُ من ذلك كُبْرَى القياس القائلة: لو قدَّرْتَ أن شيئاً من الكائنات يؤثِرُ بقوَّةٍ جعلها الله تعالى فيه لصار حينئذٍ مولانا جل وعز مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة، وقد أشار بقوله : ( وذلك باطل إلى صُغْرَاه القائلة: لكن كونه جل وعز يصيرُ مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة باطل، ثم عَلَّل ذلك بقوله: (لما عرفت... إلخ)، فصار نَظْمُ القياس هكذا: لو قَدَّرْتَ أن شيئاً من الكائنات يؤثر بقوةٍ جعلها الله تعالى فيه لصار حينئذ مولانا جل وعز مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطة، لكن كونه جل وعز يصير مفتقراً في إيجاد بعض الأفعال إلى واسطةٍ باطل لما عرفت... إلخ. (قوله: فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ... إلخ) مفرَّعٌ عن البيان السابق من قوله: (أما استغناؤه جل وعز عن كل ما سواه إلى هنا.
(قوله: تَضَمُّنَ قَوْلِ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا الله أي: تضمنَ معنى قول: لا إله إلا الله، على تقدير المضاف؛ لأن المتضمّن لذلك إنما هو المعنى لا اللفظ كما عُلِمَ مما مَرَّ. والمراد بتضمن المعنى لذلك كَوْنُه بحيث يُؤْخَذُ منه على ما تقدم بيانه، وليس المراد به دلالةَ التضمن التي هي دلالة اللفظ على جزء المعنى كما لا يخفى. (قوله: لِلْأَقْسَامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ) أي: لأنه قد اندرج تحت استغنائه تعالى عن كلّ ما سواه أَحَدَ عَشَرَ من الواجبات وهي الوجود والقدم، والبقاء، والمخالفة للحوادث والقيام بالنفس والسَّمْعُ والبصر والكلام ولوازمها كما أشار لذلك المصنف فيما تقدم بقوله: (أما استغناؤه جل وعز عن كل ما سواه فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى الوجود والقدم... إلخ)، وقد اندرج تحت افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه باقيها كما أشار إليه فيما تقدم بقوله: (وأما افتقار كلّ ما سواه إليه جل وعز فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى الحياة... إلخ)، ومعلوم أنه إذا وَجَبَتْ هذه الصفاتُ استحالَتْ أضدادها، وقد اندرج أيضاً تحت الاستغناء الجائز كما أشار إليه فيما تقدم بقوله: (ويؤخذ منه أيضاً أنه لا يجب عليه تعالى فعل شيء من الممكنات... إلخ). فتدبر.
His statement: 'Because' – meaning the state and affair. And his statement: 'He would then become' – meaning when you have supposed it influential by a power that God placed in it. And from that is taken the major premise of the syllogism: If you suppose that something from created things is influential by a power that God Almighty placed in it, then at that time our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium. And he indicated by his statement: 'And that is false' – to its minor premise stating: but His being, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium is false. Then he explained that by his statement: 'because you have known... etc.' So the arrangement of the syllogism becomes: If you suppose that something from created things is influential by a power that God Almighty placed in it, then at that time our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium, but His being, Glorified and Exalted, would become dependent in the creation of some actions upon a medium is false because you have known... etc. His statement: 'So it has become clear to you... etc.' is a branch of the previous explanation from his statement: 'As for His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him' up to here. His statement: 'the inclusion of the statement: there is no god except Allah' – meaning the inclusion of the meaning of the statement 'there is no god except Allah', on the assumption of the deleted noun; because that which includes it is only the meaning, not the wording, as is known from what has preceded. And what is meant by the inclusion of the meaning for that is its being such that it is taken from it according to what has preceded in its explanation, and it is not meant by it the 'inclusion' signification (dalalat al-tadamun) which is the signification of the wording upon part of the meaning, as is not hidden. His statement: 'for the three divisions' – meaning: because under His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, eleven of the necessary attributes have been subsumed: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, otherness from originated things, self-subsistence, hearing, sight, speech, and their consequences, as the author indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'As for His self-sufficiency, Glorified and Exalted, from everything other than Him, it necessitates for Him, Exalted, existence, pre-eternity... etc.' And under the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, the rest of them have been subsumed, as he indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'As for the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, Glorified and Exalted, it necessitates for Him, Exalted, life... etc.' And it is known that when these attributes are necessary, their opposites become impossible. And also under the permissible self-sufficiency have been subsumed, as he indicated to that in what preceded by his statement: 'And from it is also taken that it is not obligatory upon Him, Exalted, to do anything from the possible things... etc.' So reflect.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides a logical proof (qiyas) and a doctrinal derivation. First, Al-Bajuri explains the syllogism implicit in Sanusi's text: The major premise (kubra) is that if a creature influences by a God-given power, then God would become dependent on a medium for some actions. The minor premise (sughra) is that God being dependent on a medium is false (bāṭil). The conclusion is that such influence is impossible. Al-Bajuri notes that Sanusi's statement 'because you have known...' provides the justification for the minor premise. Then, Al-Bajuri turns to the phrase 'the inclusion (tadammun) of the statement: there is no god except Allah'. He clarifies that it is the meaning of the shahada, not the wording, that entails the three divisions (aqsām thalātha). This inclusion (tadammun) is not the linguistic signification of part of the meaning, but rather a logical entailment. Specifically, from God's self-sufficiency (istighnā') eleven necessary attributes are derived: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, otherness from originated things, self-subsistence, hearing, sight, speech, and their consequences. From the dependence of all else (iftiqār) on God, the remaining attributes (like life, will, power) are derived. When these attributes are necessary, their opposites become impossible. Additionally, from the permissible (jā'iz) aspect of the shahada, it follows that God is not obligated to do anything possible. Al-Bajuri concludes with 'So reflect' (fa-tadabbar), inviting the reader to contemplate the comprehensiveness of tawhid.

Key Terms
تضمن (tadammun)
أقسام ثلاثة (aqsam thalatha)
استغناء (istighna')
افتقار (iftiqar)
واسطة (wasita)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'inclusion' (tadammun) of the shahada is the same as the linguistic signification of part of the meaning (dalalat al-tadammun).
Correction: Al-Bajuri explicitly says that the inclusion here is not the linguistic signification but a logical entailment of the meaning.

Checkpoint
How many necessary attributes does Al-Bajuri say are derived from God's self-sufficiency (istighna')?
A) Ten
B) Eleven
C) Twelve
D) Thirteen

Key Takeaway
The shahada's meaning comprehensively includes the three divisions of tawhid—necessary, impossible, permissible—from which all divine attributes are derived logically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite 'La ilaha illa Allah' daily—but have you ever considered that this single sentence entails that God cannot be unjust, tired, or need anything from you? Will you pause after every shahada today to affirm His perfection in each of these three divisions?
?
If the shahada shows that God is not obligated to do anything for you (permissible division), then why do you sometimes feel entitled to His blessings? How can you transform your gratitude into true servitude?
?
The eleven necessary attributes from self-sufficiency include hearing and sight—do you live as if God hears every whisper and sees every deed? What will you change in your private moments starting now?

Spiritual Gifts Depend on Allah's Will Alone
The commentator explains that the attainment of spiritual gifts depends solely on Allah's will, and the servant's duty is worship and submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attainment of spiritual gifts is entirely dependent on Allah's will, not on the quantity of worship, and that the servant's duty is sincere worship and complete trust in Allah's decree.

Core Idea
Spiritual gifts are by Allah's will alone; our duty is worship and trust.

Sanusi includes the phrase 'if Allah wills' after mentioning the fruits of dhikr. The commentator unpacks this phrase to clarify a subtle but crucial point: the connection between worship and its results is not automatic. Even abundant remembrance may not produce the promised spiritual opening. This lesson examines why that is and what the servant's proper response should be.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the commentator's explanation of the phrase 'if Allah wills'.
Pay attention to the terms 'المعطي المانع' (the Giver, the Withholder).
2
Identify the key teaching
The passage makes two major points: (1) spiritual gifts are only by Allah's will, (2) the servant's duty is worship and submission. Locate these in the text.
3
Reflect on the comparison
The commentator compares spiritual provisions (rizq al-arwāḥ) to physical provisions (rizq al-ashbāḥ). Write down how this analogy reinforces the lesson.
Think about tawakkul in both realms.
4
Check your understanding
Take the checkpoint quiz to ensure you have grasped the core message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أشار بذلك إلى أن حصول ما ذُكِرَ إنما هو بإرادته تعالى، فهو المعطي المانِعُ، فقد يُوجَدُ إكثارُ الذِّكْرِ، ويتخلَّفُ عنه ذلك، وحينئذ فالمطلوب من العبد إنما هو القيام بالعبادة، ويُسَلِّمُ الأمور له تعالى متكلاً على قِسْمَته في أرزاق الأرواح، كما يتّكل عليه في أرزاق الأشباح.
(His statement: 'if Allah, the Exalted, wills') he indicated by that that the attainment of what was mentioned is only by His will, the Exalted. So He is the Giver, the Withholder. It may be that frequent remembrance occurs, yet that (attainment) is withheld from it. And then what is required of the servant is only the performance of worship, and he entrusts matters to Him, the Exalted, relying on His division in the provisions of spirits, just as he relies on Him in the provisions of bodies.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'If Allah wills' (in shāʾa Allāh) from Sanusi’s text. The commentator clarifies that the attainment of spiritual secrets and miracles is entirely dependent upon Allah’s will. Allah is the sole Giver and Withholder. It is possible that a person increases in remembrance (dhikr) yet does not receive those gifts. Therefore, the servant’s duty is simply to perform worship and to entrust all outcomes to Allah, relying on His distribution in the provisions of souls (arāq al-arwāḥ) just as one relies on His distribution of physical provisions (arāq al-ashbāḥ). This underscores tawakkul (trust) in both spiritual and material sustenance.

Key Terms
إرادته
المعطي المانع
تسليم
توكل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person might think that performing more dhikr automatically guarantees spiritual gifts like unveiling or closeness to Allah.
Correction: The commentator explains that even frequent dhikr can be performed without the desired result because the gift is granted solely by Allah's will, not earned by quantity of worship. The servant's duty is to worship sincerely and submit to Allah's decree, not to expect specific outcomes.

Checkpoint

A) Increase remembrance until gifts are given
B) Question Allah’s will
C) Continue worship and submit to Allah’s decree
D) Seek the gifts by other means

Key Takeaway
Spiritual gifts are solely at Allah’s disposal; the servant’s responsibility is worship and complete trust in His distribution of all provisions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in worship, do you secretly calculate what spiritual benefit you expect to receive? How would your worship change if you truly performed it with no expectation of a gift, only out of duty to Allah?
?
Do you trust Allah's distribution of spiritual graces—like stillness of heart or closeness to Him—as completely as you trust Him for your next meal? In what specific area of your spiritual life do you find yourself clinging to control rather than entrusting?
?
If Allah were to withhold every spiritual feeling you desire, would you still be content to worship Him? Surrender to Him right now the one spiritual gift you are most afraid of never receiving.

Exclusivity of Tawfiq to Allah
Al-Bajuri argues for the exclusivity of tawfiq to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why tawfiq (divine assistance) is exclusive to Allah and why no additional phrase is needed to exclude the disbeliever.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is the power for obedience, absent in disbelievers, so only Allah grants it.

In this passage, al-Bajuri clarifies a key point about tawfiq: it is the divine assistance that enables obedience, and it is inherently absent in the disbeliever. He argues against a scholarly addition to the definition, showing why it is unnecessary. Read on to see his concise reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once. Notice how al-Bajuri defines the 'accident accompanying obedience' and its absence in the disbeliever.
2
Identify the logical argument
The passage presents a simple deduction: since the accident accompanying obedience is absent in the disbeliever, the additional phrase is redundant. Follow the reasoning.
The accident is the power (quwwa) that enables obedience.
3
Reflect on theological implications
Consider why this matters: tawfiq is a divine act exclusive to Allah. This excludes any notion of independent power in creation.
This connects to the broader kalam principle of divine omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العَرَضُ المُقارِنُ للطاعة، وذلك غير موجود في الكافر لعدم وجود الطاعة منه، وبهذا كُلَّه تَعْلَمُ أنه لا حاجة لزيادة بعضهم وتسهيل سبيل الخير إليه لإخراج الكافر. فتأمل. (قوله: لَا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ) خبر (لا) محذوف والتقدير لا رب غيره موجود، والجملة مستأنفة استئنافاً بيانياً، وهو الواقع في جواب سؤال مقدرٍ، فكأن سائلاً قال للمصنف : لِمَ قصرت التوفيق على كونه الله تعالى؟ فأجاب بأنه لا رَبَّ غيرُه.
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: الْعَرَضُ الْمُقَارِنُ) وهو القوة المصاحبة للطاعة، ومعلوم أن القوة لا تكون إلا بسلامة الآلات
(قوله: خَبَرُ لَا مَحْذُوف) ويصلح أن يكون خبرها لفظ (غير)، فيكون مرفوعاً على الخبرية، ولا حذف، والله أعلم.
The accident accompanying obedience is not present in the disbeliever due to the absence of obedience from him, and by all this you know that there is no need for the addition of some of them [i.e., the scholars] of 'and facilitating the path of good to him' to exclude the disbeliever. So ponder. (His words: 'There is no lord other than Him') The predicate of 'la' is omitted, and the estimation is: there is no lord other than Him existing, and the sentence is a resumptive explanatory sentence, and it occurs as the answer to an implied question, as if a questioner said to the author: 'Why did you restrict tawfiq to being from Allah?' So he answered: 'Because there is no lord other than Him.' Marginal note of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: (His words: 'The accident accompanying [obedience]') It is the power accompanying obedience, and it is known that power is only with soundness of instruments. (His words: 'The predicate of 'la' is omitted') And it is possible that its predicate is the word 'ghayr' (other), so it would be raised as a predicate, and there is no omission, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the issue of tawfiq (divine assistance) and the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu'. The author begins by stating that the 'accident accompanying obedience' (al-'arad al-muqarin lil-ta'ah) is not present in the disbeliever because he does not have obedience. This implies that tawfiq, which is the power (quwwa) that enables obedience, is only given to believers. He notes that some scholars added 'and facilitating the path of good to him' to the definition of tawfiq to exclude the disbeliever, but the author says this is unnecessary because the disbeliever already lacks obedience. Then he explains the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu' grammatically: the predicate of 'la' is omitted, estimated as 'exists'. The sentence is a resumptive explanatory sentence answering an implied question: why restrict tawfiq to Allah? The answer is that there is no other lord. Then al-Ajhuri's marginal note clarifies that 'the accident accompanying' is the power that comes with obedience, and power requires sound instruments. Another note discusses the grammatical possibility that 'ghayr' itself could be the predicate of 'la', raising it as a predicate without omission. The passage thus combines theological and linguistic analysis.

Key Terms
tawfiq
al-'arad al-muqarin
al-ta'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawfiq can be granted by other than Allah, or that a special phrase is needed to exclude disbelievers from tawfiq.
Correction: Tawfiq is the power for obedience, and since disbelievers lack obedience, they automatically lack tawfiq. No extra phrase is needed.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why is there no need for the addition 'and facilitating the path of good to him' to the definition of tawfiq?
A) Because the disbeliever already has tawfiq from other sources.
B) Because the accident accompanying obedience is absent in the disbeliever.
C) Because the addition is grammatically incorrect.
D) Because the disbeliever has no instruments.

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq is the God-given power for obedience, inherently absent in disbelievers, so no extra exclusion is needed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in an act of worship, do you attribute that ability to your own effort or to Allah’s tawfiq? How will you remind yourself daily that obedience is a gift?
?
If tawfiq is absent in disbelievers, how should this shape your dua for their guidance? What does it teach you about your own need for constant tawfiq?
?
Think of a time you fell into sin. Did you consider that you were lacking tawfiq in that moment? How can this lesson transform your repentance and reliance on Allah for future obedience?

Grammatical Analysis of 'La Rabba Ghayruhu'
Al-Bajuri and al-Ajhuri analyze the grammar of 'la rabba ghayruhu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical structure of the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu' and the two possible analyses of its predicate.

Core Idea
The phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu' has an omitted predicate or a raised predicate, both grammatically valid.

Al-Bajuri examines the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu' (there is no lord other than Him) both theologically and grammatically. He explains that it answers an implied question about the exclusivity of tawfiq. Then al-Ajhuri's marginal notes add two grammatical points: the nature of the 'accident accompanying' and the possibility that 'ghayr' itself is the predicate. Let's explore these linguistic insights.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the main text and the two marginal notes. Notice how the grammar is discussed in relation to the theological meaning.
2
Understand the implied question
Al-Bajuri explains that the sentence is a resumptive answer to an implied question: 'Why did you restrict tawfiq to Allah?' The answer is that there is no other lord.
This connects grammar to theology.
3
Analyze the two grammatical possibilities
The first possibility: the predicate of 'la' is omitted (estimated as 'exists'). The second (from al-Ajhuri): 'ghayr' itself is the predicate, so it is raised (marfu') and no omission occurs.
Both interpretations are valid in Arabic grammar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العَرَضُ المُقارِنُ للطاعة، وذلك غير موجود في الكافر لعدم وجود الطاعة منه، وبهذا كُلَّه تَعْلَمُ أنه لا حاجة لزيادة بعضهم وتسهيل سبيل الخير إليه لإخراج الكافر. فتأمل. (قوله: لَا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ) خبر (لا) محذوف والتقدير لا رب غيره موجود، والجملة مستأنفة استئنافاً بيانياً، وهو الواقع في جواب سؤال مقدرٍ، فكأن سائلاً قال للمصنف : لِمَ قصرت التوفيق على كونه الله تعالى؟ فأجاب بأنه لا رَبَّ غيرُه.
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري

(قوله: خَبَرُ لَا مَحْذُوف) ويصلح أن يكون خبرها لفظ (غير)، فيكون مرفوعاً على الخبرية، ولا حذف، والله أعلم.

This passage is a commentary on the issue of tawfiq (divine assistance) and the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu'. This implies that tawfiq, which is the power (quwwa) that enables obedience, is only given to believers. He notes that some scholars added 'and facilitating the path of good to him' to the definition of tawfiq to exclude the disbeliever, but the author says this is unnecessary because the disbeliever already lacks obedience. Then he explains the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu' grammatically: the predicate of 'la' is omitted, estimated as 'exists'. The sentence is a resumptive explanatory sentence answering an implied question: why restrict tawfiq to Allah? The answer is that there is no other lord. Then al-Ajhuri's marginal note clarifies that 'the accident accompanying' is the power that comes with obedience, and power requires sound instruments. Another note discusses the grammatical possibility that 'ghayr' itself could be the predicate of 'la', raising it as a predicate without omission. The passage thus combines theological and linguistic analysis.

Key Terms
la rabba ghayruhu
al-quwwa
khabar

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the predicate of 'la' must always be omitted in such constructions.
Correction: Al-Ajhuri shows that 'ghayr' can serve as the predicate, with no omission needed.

Checkpoint
What is the alternative grammatical analysis presented by al-Ajhuri for the phrase 'la rabba ghayruhu'?
A) The word 'rabba' is the predicate.
B) The word 'ghayr' is the predicate and is raised (marfu').
C) The word 'mawjud' is the predicate.
D) The predicate is omitted and cannot be identified.

Key Takeaway
The grammar of 'la rabba ghayruhu' admits two valid analyses, both reinforcing the theological truth that Allah alone is Lord.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear 'la rabba ghayruhu', do you pause to consider that no other being truly has lordship over your life? In what area of your life are you acting as if there is a 'lord' besides Allah? What would it look like to consciously affirm this truth in that area today?
?
The grammatical discussion shows that even a small detail can reinforce tawhid. How often do you reflect on the linguistic nuances of Islamic statements of faith? Could a deeper understanding of Arabic increase your certainty and reverence for Allah? Make a commitment to learn one new Arabic term related to tawhid this week.
